# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Investigation: Django ADMINS/MANAGERS Settings Format Migration Audit

**Repository:** django/django
**Task Type:** Migration Audit (investigation only — no code changes)

## Scenario

Django is changing the `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from their current format of `[(name, email), ...]` tuples to simple `[email, ...]` string lists. This is tracked in ticket #36138. Before executing this migration, the team needs a comprehensive audit of all code that reads, validates, or processes these settings.

## Your Task

Produce a migration audit report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Every file that reads `settings.ADMINS` or `settings.MANAGERS`
2. Every file that validates or type-checks the settings format
3. Every file that unpacks the tuple format (e.g., `for name, email in settings.ADMINS`)
4. All documentation references that show the old tuple format
5. Test files that use the old format in fixtures or assertions
6. Third-party compatibility concerns (what breaks for users with old-format settings)
7. A migration checklist: each file that needs changes, what change is needed

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Core code paths that consume the tuple format>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of modules/packages impacted>

## Recommendation
<Migration checklist with specific files and changes needed>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `django/core/mail/`, test files, and documentation

This is a security measure to prevent :ref:`HTTP Host header attacks\n72: <host-headers-virtual-hosting>`, which are possible even under many\n73: seemingly-safe web server configurations.\n74: \n75: Values in this list can be fully qualified names (e.g. ``'www.example.com'``),\n76: in which case they will be matched against the request's ``Host`` header\n77: exactly (case-insensitive, not including port). A value beginning with a period\n78: can be used as a subdomain wildcard: ``'.example.com'`` will match\n79: ``example.com``, ``www.example.com``, and any other subdomain of\n80: ``example.com``. 88-assistanttext-
The investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here is a summary of findings:

---

## Key Findings

**Current state (Django 6.0):** The migration is already in progress. The old `[(name, email), ...]` tuple format is deprecated with `RemovedInDjango70Warning`; removal is scheduled for Django 7.0.

**Where the tuple-format compatibility shim lives:**
- Entirely in `django/core/mail/__init__.py:165–173` inside `_send_server_message()`. This is the only place that reads `a[1]` from the tuples. No other code in Django ever used the `name` portion.

**Code paths that consume the settings:**
1. `_send_server_message()` (`django/core/mail/__init__.py`) — reads, detects old format, warns, extracts email
2. `AdminEmailHandler.emit()` (`django/utils/log.py:97`) — only a truthiness check (`if not settings.ADMINS`)
3. `BrokenLinkEmailsMiddleware` (`django/middleware/common.py`) — calls `mail_managers()` which routes through the shim

**What needs to change for Django 7.0:**
1. **`django/core/mail/__init__.py`** — Delete the 9-line backward-compat block in `_send_server_message()`
2. **`tests/mail/tests.py`** — Delete `test_deprecated_admins_managers_tuples`; uncomment two error-case assertions in `test_wrong_admins_managers`
3. **`docs/ref/settings.txt`** — Remove `versionchanged:: 6.0` notes under `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS`
4. **`docs/internals/deprecation.txt`** — Remove the Django 7.0 deprecation entry for tuple support
5. **`docs/releases/7.0.txt`** — Add removal notice

**Third-party impact:** Any project with `ADMINS = [("Name", "email@example.com"), ...]` will break. The fix is dropping the name: `ADMINS = ["email@example.com"]`. No functional behavior changes since the name was never displayed or used.

When\\n51: :setting:`DEBUG=False <DEBUG>` and :class:`~django.utils.log.AdminEmailHandler`\\n52: is configured in :setting:`LOGGING` (done by default), Django emails these\\n53: people the details of exceptions raised in the request/response cycle.\\n54: \\n55: Each item in the list should be an email address string. Example::\\n56: \\n57:     ADMINS = [\\\"john@example.com\\\", '\\\"Ng, Mary\\\" <mary@example.com>']\\n58: \\n59: .. versionchanged:: 6.0\\n60: \\n61:     In older versions, required a list of (name, address) tuples.\\n62: \\n63: .. setting:: ALLOWED_HOSTS\\n64: \\n65: ``ALLOWED_HOSTS``\\n66: -----------------\\n67: \\n68: Default: ``[]`` (Empty list)\\n69: \\n70: A list of strings representing the host/domain names that this Django site can\\n71: serve. This is a security measure to prevent :ref:`HTTP Host header attacks\\n72: <host-headers-virtual-hosting>`, which are possible even under many\\n73: seemingly-safe web server configurations.\\n74: \\n75: Values in this list can be fully qualified names (e.g. ``'www.example.com'``),\\n76: in which case they will be matched against the request's ``Host`` header\\n77: exactly (case-insensitive, not including port). A value beginning with a period\\n78: can be used as a subdomain wildcard: ``'.example.com'`` will match\\n79: ``example.com``, ``www.example.com``, and any other subdomain of\\n80: ``example.com``. A value of ``'*'`` will match anything; in this case you are\\n81: responsible to provide your own validation of the ``Host`` header (perhaps in a\\n82: middleware; if so this middleware must be listed first in\\n83: :setting:`MIDDLEWARE`).\\n84: \\n85: Django also allows the `fully qualified domain name (FQDN)`_ of any entries.\\n86: Some browsers include a trailing dot in the ``Host`` header which Django\\n87: strips when performing host validation.\\n88: \\n89: .. _`fully qualified domain name (FQDN)`: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fully_qualified_domain_name\\n90: \\n91: If the ``Host`` header (or ``X-Forwarded-Host`` if\\n92: :setting:`USE_X_FORWARDED_HOST` is enabled) does not match any value in this\\n93: list, the :meth:`django.http.HttpRequest.get_host` method will raise\\n94: :exc:`~django.core.exceptions.SuspiciousOperation`.\\n95: \\n96: When :setting:`DEBUG` is ``True`` and ``ALLOWED_HOSTS`` is empty, the host\\n97: is validated against ``['.localhost', '127.0.0.1', '[::1]']``.\\n98: \\n99: ``ALLOWED_HOSTS`` is also :ref:`checked when running tests\\n100: <topics-testing-advanced-multiple-hosts>`.\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/django/django@4513a6c2a9694b3da144846f3edfa1c3673a181d/-/blob/docs/ref/settings.txt%3FL42-100\"}",

  "content": "# Investigation Report\n\n## Summary\n\nDjango is actively migrating `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from the old `[(name, email), ...]` tuple-list format to simple `[email, ...]` string lists. As of Django 6.0, the old tuple format is deprecated with a `RemovedInDjango70Warning`; it will be removed in Django 7.0. The deprecation shim currently lives in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` in the `_send_server_message()` helper. All Django-internal code and tests have already been updated to use the new string-list format \u2014 the remaining work is removing the backward-compatibility shim and the associated deprecated-format test coverage.\n\n---\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe core code path is:\n\n1. `mail_admins()` / `mail_managers()` in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` both delegate to `_send_server_message()`.\n2. `_send_server_message()` reads `settings.ADMINS` or `settings.MANAGERS`, then:\n   - Checks whether every item is a 2-element list/tuple (`isinstance(a, (list, tuple)) and len(a) == 2`).\n   - If yes, emits `RemovedInDjango70Warning` and extracts only the second element (the email address): `recipients = [a[1] for a in recipients]`.\n   - If no (and the value is not a flat list of strings), raises `ImproperlyConfigured`.\n3. `AdminEmailHandler.emit()` in `django/utils/log.py` has an early-return guard: `if not settings.ADMINS` \u2014 this works correctly for both old and new format since truthiness is unchanged.\n4. `BrokenLinkEmailsMiddleware` in `django/middleware/common.py` calls `mail_managers()` which in turn goes through the same `_send_server_message()` path.\n\nThe tuple-format support is entirely encapsulated inside `_send_server_message()` \u2014 there is no other place that unpacks `(name, email)` pairs directly from the settings. The name component was never used anywhere in the Django codebase.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Files that read `settings.ADMINS` or `settings.MANAGERS`\n\n| File | Line(s) | How it reads the setting |\n|------|---------|--------------------------|\n| `django/core/mail/__init__.py` | 161, 166\u2013173 | `getattr(settings, setting_name)` \u2014 then unpacks with `a[1]` if tuple-format detected |\n| `django/utils/log.py` | 97 | `if not settings.ADMINS` \u2014 truthiness guard only, no tuple unpacking |\n| `django/conf/global_settings.py` | 26, 175 | Defines defaults: `ADMINS = []`, `MANAGERS = ADMINS` |\n\n### Files that validate or type-check the settings format\n\n| File | Lines | What it checks |\n|------|-------|----------------|\n| `django/core/mail/__init__.py` | 166\u2013180 | Old-format detection (`all(isinstance(a, (list,tuple)) and len(a)==2 ...)`), then new-format validation (`isinstance(address, (str, Promise))`), raises `ImproperlyConfigured` on mismatch |\n\n### The deprecation shim \u2014 key code excerpt\n\n`django/core/mail/__init__.py`, lines 165\u2013180:\n\n```python\n# RemovedInDjango70Warning.\nif all(isinstance(a, (list, tuple)) and len(a) == 2 for a in recipients):\n    warnings.warn(\n        f\"Using (name, address) pairs in the {setting_name} setting is deprecated.\"\n        \" Replace with a list of email address strings.\",\n        RemovedInDjango70Warning,\n        stacklevel=2,\n    )\n    recipients = [a[1] for a in recipients]\n\nif not isinstance(recipients, (list, tuple)) or not all(\n    isinstance(address, (str, Promise)) for address in recipients\n):\n    raise ImproperlyConfigured(\n        f\"The {setting_name} setting must be a list of email address strings.\"\n    )\n```\n\n### Files that unpack the tuple format (the `a[1]` pattern)\n\nOnly one location performs actual tuple unpacking:\n\n- `django/core/mail/__init__.py:173`: `recipients = [a[1] for a in recipients]`\n\nThere is no other tuple-unpacking of `ADMINS` / `MANAGERS` anywhere in the codebase. The historical pattern `for name, email in settings.ADMINS` does **not** appear; Django never used the `name` portion in any functional code path.\n\n### Documentation references showing old or new format\n\n| File | Lines | Content |\n|------|-------|---------|\n| `docs/ref/settings.txt` | 55\u201361 | `ADMINS` entry now shows new string format; `versionchanged:: 6.0` note says \"In older versions, required a list of (name, address) tuples.\" |\n| `docs/ref/settings.txt` | 2081\u20132087 | `MANAGERS` entry mirrors same format change and versionchanged note |\n| `docs/internals/deprecation.txt` | 34\u201335 | \"Support for setting the `ADMINS` or `MANAGERS` settings to a list of (name, address) tuples will be removed.\" |\n| `docs/releases/6.0.txt` | 538\u2013541 | Deprecation notice: `\"Setting ADMINS or MANAGERS to a list of (name, address) tuples is deprecated.\"` |\n| `docs/howto/error-reporting.txt` | 21\u201345 | Now describes `ADMINS` as a list of email addresses (no tuples) |\n| `django/conf/global_settings.py` | 25 | Comment updated to new format: `# [\"email@example.com\", '\"Full Name\" <anotheremail@example.com>']` |\n\n### Test files using the old format (deprecated, marked `RemovedInDjango70Warning`)\n\n| File | Lines | What it tests |\n|------|-------|---------------|\n| `tests/mail/tests.py` | 2403\u20132426 | `test_deprecated_admins_managers_tuples` \u2014 explicitly tests that `[(\"nobody\", \"nobody@example.com\"), ...]` triggers the deprecation warning and still delivers email to the address portion |\n| `tests/mail/tests.py` | 2432\u20132441 | Commented-out cases in `test_wrong_admins_managers` \u2014 tuple-pair inputs that should raise `ImproperlyConfigured` once the deprecation shim is removed |\n\n### Test files already using the new string-list format\n\n| File | Lines | Setting value |\n|------|-------|---------------|\n| `tests/mail/tests.py` | 1364 | `ADMINS=[\"nobody@example.com\"]` |\n| `tests/mail/tests.py` | 1377 | `MANAGERS=[\"nobody@example.com\"]` |\n| `tests/mail/tests.py` | 2320\u20132343 | `test_mail_admins_and_managers` \u2014 new-format matrix with strings, lazy strings |\n| `tests/mail/tests.py` | 2345 | `@override_settings(MANAGERS=[\"nobody@example.com\"])` |\n| `tests/mail/tests.py` | 2360 | `@override_settings(ADMINS=[\"nobody@example.com\"])` |\n| `tests/logging_tests/tests.py` | 439 | `MANAGERS=[\"manager@example.com\"]` |\n| `tests/logging_tests/tests.py` | 481 | `ADMINS=[\"admin@example.com\"]` |\n| `tests/logging_tests/tests.py` | 495 | `ADMINS=[\"admin@example.com\"]` |\n| `tests/logging_tests/tests.py` | 517 | `ADMINS=[]` |\n| `tests/logging_tests/tests.py` | 613 | `ADMINS=[\"admin@example.com\"]` |\n| `tests/middleware/tests.py` | 406 | `MANAGERS=[\"manager@example.com\"]` |\n\n---\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`django/core/mail/__init__.py`** \u2014 primary location of the deprecation shim inside `_send_server_message()`. This is the only file that needs a functional code change to complete the migration.\n\n2. **`django/conf/global_settings.py`** \u2014 defines `ADMINS = []` and `MANAGERS = ADMINS`; already uses new format in its comment. No functional change required.\n\n3. **`django/utils/log.py` (`AdminEmailHandler`)** \u2014 reads `settings.ADMINS` only as a truthiness guard; does not unpack the format. No change required.\n\n4. **`django/middleware/common.py` (`BrokenLinkEmailsMiddleware`)** \u2014 calls `mail_managers()`, which handles format through the shared shim. No direct change required.\n\n5. **`django/core/management/commands/sendtestemail.py`** \u2014 calls `mail_managers()` and `mail_admins()` directly; no format awareness. No change required.\n\n6. **`tests/mail/tests.py`** \u2014 contains the deprecated-format test (`test_deprecated_admins_managers_tuples`) and commented-out error cases that need to be uncommented after removal.\n\n7. **Documentation files** (already updated for 6.0 with versionchanged notes):\n   - `docs/ref/settings.txt`\n   - `docs/releases/6.0.txt`\n   - `docs/internals/deprecation.txt`\n   - `docs/howto/error-reporting.txt`\n\n---\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Migration Checklist for Django 7.0\n\n**`django/core/mail/__init__.py`** \u2014 _Primary code change_\n\n- [ ] Remove the `RemovedInDjango70Warning` tuple-detection block in `_send_server_message()` (lines 165\u2013173):\n  ```python\n  # DELETE this entire block:\n  if all(isinstance(a, (list, tuple)) and len(a) == 2 for a in recipients):\n      warnings.warn(...)\n      recipients = [a[1] for a in recipients]\n  ```\n- [ ] The remaining format validation (`isinstance(recipients, (list, tuple)) or not all(isinstance(address, (str, Promise)) ...)`) can be kept or simplified as the new canonical check.\n- [ ] Remove the `# RemovedInDjango70Warning.` comment on line 165.\n\n**`tests/mail/tests.py`** \u2014 _Test cleanup_\n\n- [ ] Delete the entire `test_deprecated_admins_managers_tuples` method (lines 2402\u20132426), which exists only to validate the now-removed backward-compatibility shim.\n- [ ] In `test_wrong_admins_managers` (line 2428), uncomment the two tuple-pair test cases (lines 2432\u20132441) so that `[(\"nobody\", \"nobody@example.com\"), ...]` and `[[\"nobody\", \"nobody@example.com\"], ...]` now correctly raise `ImproperlyConfigured`.\n\n**`docs/ref/settings.txt`** \u2014 _Documentation cleanup_\n\n- [ ] Remove the `.. versionchanged:: 6.0` block under 7.0\" section noting the removal of tuple support for `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS`, with a pointer back to the Django 6.0 deprecation.\n\n### Third-party compatibility concerns\n\nAny Django project that The fix is straightforward \u2014 drop the name string:\n\n```python\n# Old (breaks in Django 7.0)\nADMINS = [(\"John\", \"john@example.com\"), (\"Mary\", \"mary@example.com\")]\n\n# New (works in Django 6.0+)\nADMINS = [\"john@example.com\", '\"Mary\" <mary@example.com>']\n```\n\nSince Django never used the `name` portion in any email or UI, dropping it has no functional impact. The `email.utils.formataddr()` function can be used to embed a display name inside the email address string if needed.\n\nThe deprecation warning (`RemovedInDjango70Warning`) is the signal for third-party package maintainers and application developers to migrate. No Django-internal code that calls `mail_admins()` or `mail_managers()` passes the settings value directly \u2014 all callers go through the `_send_server_message()` helper, so the shim is the only migration surface.\n",

The fix is straightforward \u2014 drop the name string:\n\n```python\n# Old (breaks in Django 7.0)\nADMINS = [(\"John\", \"john@example.com\"), (\"Mary\", \"mary@example.com\")]\n\n# New (works in Django 6.0+)\nADMINS = [\"john@example.com\", '\"Mary\" <mary@example.com>']\n```\n\nSince Django never used the `name` portion in any email or UI, dropping it has no functional impact. The `email.utils.formataddr()` function can be used to embed a display name inside the email address string if needed.\n\nThe deprecation warning (`RemovedInDjango70Warning`) is the signal for third-party package maintainers and application developers to migrate. No Django-internal code that calls `mail_admins()` or `mail_managers()` passes the settings value directly \u2014 all callers go through the `_send_server_message()` helper, so the shim is the only migration surface.\n",

# Investigation Report

## Summary

Django is actively migrating `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from the old `[(name, email), ...]` tuple-list format to simple `[email, ...]` string lists. As of Django 6.0, the old tuple format is deprecated with a `RemovedInDjango70Warning`; it will be removed in Django 7.0. The deprecation shim currently lives in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` in the `_send_server_message()` helper. All Django-internal code and tests have already been updated to use the new string-list format — the remaining work is removing the backward-compatibility shim and the associated deprecated-format test coverage.

---

## Root Cause

The core code path is:

1. `mail_admins()` / `mail_managers()` in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` both delegate to `_send_server_message()`.
2. `_send_server_message()` reads `settings.ADMINS` or `settings.MANAGERS`, then:
   - Checks whether every item is a 2-element list/tuple (`isinstance(a, (list, tuple)) and len(a) == 2`).
   - If yes, emits `RemovedInDjango70Warning` and extracts only the second element (the email address): `recipients = [a[1] for a in recipients]`.
   - If no (and the value is not a flat list of strings), raises `ImproperlyConfigured`.
3. `AdminEmailHandler.emit()` in `django/utils/log.py` has an early-return guard: `if not settings.ADMINS` — this works correctly for both old and new format since truthiness is unchanged.
4. `BrokenLinkEmailsMiddleware` in `django/middleware/common.py` calls `mail_managers()` which in turn goes through the same `_send_server_message()` path.

The tuple-format support is entirely encapsulated inside `_send_server_message()` — there is no other place that unpacks `(name, email)` pairs directly from the settings. The name component was never used anywhere in the Django code
... (truncated)
